with <a href="/wiki/Sirius" title="Sirius">Sirius</a> near <a href="/wiki/Betelgeuse" title="Betelgeuse">Betelgeuse</a>, <a href="/wiki/Procyon" title="Procyon">Procyon</a> in <a href="/wiki/Gemini_(constellation)" title="Gemini (constellation)">Gemini</a>, and the <a href="/wiki/Sun" title="Sun">Sun</a> in <a href="/wiki/Cassiopeia_(constellation)" title="Cassiopeia (constellation)">Cassiopeia</a> generated by <a href="/wiki/Celestia" title="Celestia">Celestia</a></div></div></div>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:282px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Sun_from_Alpha_Centauri.png"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="424" data-file-width="706" decoding="async" height="168" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8a/Sun_from_Alpha_Centauri.png/280px-Sun_from_Alpha_Centauri.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8a/Sun_from_Alpha_Centauri.png/420px-Sun_from_Alpha_Centauri.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8a/Sun_from_Alpha_Centauri.png/560px-Sun_from_Alpha_Centauri.png 2x" width="280"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Sun_from_Alpha_Centauri.png" title="Enlarge"></a></div>The Sun in the constellation <a href="/wiki/Cassiopeia_(constellation)" title="Cassiopeia (constellation)">Cassiopeia</a> as seen from Alpha Centauri</div></div></div>\n<p>The sky from Alpha Centauri AB would appear much as it does from the <a href="/wiki/Earth" title="Earth">Earth</a>, except that <a href="/wiki/Centaurus" title="Centaurus">Centaurus</a> would be missing its brightest star. The <a href="/wiki/Sun" title="Sun">Sun</a> would appear as a yellow star of <a href="/wiki/Apparent_magnitude" title="Apparent magnitude">apparent magnitude</a> +0.5, roughly the same as the average brightness of <a href="/wiki/Betelgeuse" title="Betelgeuse">Betelgeuse</a> from Earth. It would be at the <a href="/wiki/Antipodal_point" title="Antipodal point">antipodal point</a> of Alpha Centauri AB\'s current <a href="/wiki/Right_ascension" title="Right ascension">right ascension</a> and <a href="/wiki/Declination" title="Declination">declination</a>, at &#160;02<sup>h</sup>&#160;39<sup>m</sup>&#160;35<sup>s</sup> +60&#176;&#160;50&#8242; (2000), in eastern <a href="/wiki/Cassiopeia_(constellation)" title="Cassiopeia (constellation)">Cassiopeia</a>, easily outshining all the rest of the stars in the <a href="/wiki/Constellation" title="Constellation">constellation</a>. With the placement of the Sun east of the 3.4-magnitude star <a href="/wiki/Epsilon_Cassiopeiae" title="Epsilon Cassiopeiae">&#949; Cassiopeiae</a>, it would be nearly in front of the <a href="/wiki/Heart_Nebula" title="Heart Nebula">Heart Nebula</a>, and the "W" of Cassiopeia would appear as a "/W" shape.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-108"><a href="#cite_note-108">[note 7]</a></sup>\n</p><p>The <a href="/wiki/Winter_Triangle" title="Winter Triangle">Winter Triangle</a> would have a very different appearance, with <a href="/wiki/Procyon" title="Procyon">Procyon</a> outshining <a href="/wiki/Pollux_(star)" title="Pollux (star)">Pollux</a> in the middle of <a href="/wiki/Gemini_(constellation)" title="Gemini (constellation)">Gemini</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Sirius" title="Sirius">Sirius</a> lying less than a degree from Betelgeuse in <a href="/wiki/Orion_(constellation)" title="Orion (constellation)">Orion</a>. With a magnitude of &#8722;1.2, Sirius would be a little fainter than from Earth but still the brightest star in the night sky. Both <a href="/wiki/Vega" title="Vega">Vega</a> and <a href="/wiki/Altair" title="Altair">Altair</a> would be shifted northwestward relative to <a href="/wiki/Deneb" title="Deneb">Deneb</a>, giving the <a href="/wiki/Summer_Triangle" title="Summer Triangle">Summer Triangle</a> a more <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Equilateral" title="Equilateral">equilateral</a> appearance.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (January 2019)">citation needed</span></a></i>]</sup>\n</p><p>Alpha Centauri is inside the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/G-cloud" title="G-cloud">G-cloud</a>, and its nearest known system is the binary <a href="/wiki/Brown_dwarf" title="Brown dwarf">brown dwarf</a> system <a href="/wiki/Luhman_16" title="Luhman 16">Luhman 16</a> at 3.6&#160;ly (1.1&#160;pc).<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-substellarcompanion_109-0"><a href="#cite_note-substellarcompanion-109">[102]</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Other_names">Other names</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Alpha_Centauri&amp;action=edit&amp;section=20" title="Edit section: Other names">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>\n<p>In modern literature, <i>Rigil Kent</i><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-110"><a href="#cite_note-110">[103]</a></sup> (also <i>Rigel Kent</i> and variants;<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-111"><a href="#cite_note-111">[note 8]</a></sup> <span class="nowrap"><span class="IPA nopopups noexcerpt"><a href="/wiki/Help:IPA/English" title="Help:IPA/English">/<span style="border-bottom:1px dotted"><span title="/&#712;/: primary stress follows">&#712;</span><span title="\'r\' in \'rye\'">r</span><span title="/a&#618;/: \'i\' in \'tide\'">a&#618;</span><span title="/d&#658;/: \'j\' in \'jam\'">d&#658;</span><span title="/&#601;l/: \'le\' in \'bottle\'">&#601;l</span></span> <wbr/><span style="border-bottom:1px dotted"><span title="/&#712;/: primary stress follows">&#712;</span><span title="\'k\' in \'kind\'">k</span><span title="/&#603;/: \'e\' in \'dress\'">&#603;</span><span title="\'n\' in \'nigh\'">n</span><span title="\'t\' in \'tie\'">t</span></span>/</a></span></span>)<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-K&amp;S_20-1"><a href="#cite_note-K&amp;S-20">[19]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-112"><a href="#cite_note-112">[104]</a></sup> and <i>Toliman</i>,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-113"><a href="#cite_note-113">[105]</a></sup> are used as colloquial alternative names of Alpha Centauri (then became the proper name of Alpha Centauri B in 10 August 2018 by approval of <a href="/wiki/International_Astronomical_Union" title="International Astronomical Union">IAU</a>).\n</p><p><i>Rigil Kent</i> is short for <i>Rigil Kentaurus</i>,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-114"><a href="#cite_note-114">[106]</a></sup> which is sometimes further abbreviated to <i>Rigil</i> or <i>Rigel</i>, though that is ambiguous with <a href="/wiki/Rigel" title="Rigel">&#946; Orionis</a>, which is also called Rigel.\n</p><p>The name <i>Toliman</i> originates with <a href="/wiki/Jacobus_Golius" title="Jacobus Golius">Jacobus Golius</a>\' 1669 edition of <a href="/wiki/Ahmad_ibn_Muhammad_ibn_Kathir_al-Farghani" title="Ahmad ibn Muhammad ibn Kathir al-Farghani">Al-Farghani</a>\'s <i>Compendium</i>. <i>Tolim&#226;n</i> is Golius\' latinisation of the Arabic name  <span dir="rtl" lang="ar" title="Arabic language text">&#1575;&#1604;&#1592;&#1604;&#1605;&#1575;&#1606;</span>&#8206; <i lang="ar-Latn" title="Arabic language text">al-&#7826;ulm&#257;n</i> "the ostriches", the name of an asterism of which Alpha Centauri formed the main star.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-115"><a href="#cite_note-115">[107]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-116"><a href="#cite_note-116">[108]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-117"><a href="#cite_note-117">[109]</a></sup>\n</p><p>During the 19th&#160;century, the northern amateur popularist Elijah H. Burritt used the now-obscure name <i>Bungula</i>,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-118"><a href="#cite_note-118">[110]</a></sup> possibly coined from "&#946;" and the <a href="/wiki/Latin" title="Latin">Latin</a> <i>ungula</i> ("hoof").<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-K&amp;S_20-2"><a href="#cite_note-K&amp;S-20">[19]</a></sup>\n</p><p>Together, Alpha and Beta Centauri form the "Southern Pointers" or "The Pointers", as they point towards the Southern Cross, the <a href="/wiki/Asterism_(astronomy)" title="Asterism (astronomy)">asterism</a> of the constellation of <a href="/wiki/Crux" title="Crux">Crux</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-AOST2_79-1"><a href="#cite_note-AOST2-79">[74]</a></sup>\n</p><p>In <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Standard_Mandarin_Chinese" title="Standard Mandarin Chinese">Standard Mandarin Chinese</a>, <span lang="zh" title="Chinese language text">&#21335;&#38272;</span> <i>N&#225;n M&#233;n</i>, meaning <i><a href="/wiki/Horn_(Chinese_constellation)" title="Horn (Chinese constellation)">Southern Gate</a></i>, refers to an asterism consisting of &#945;&#160;Centauri and <a href="/wiki/Epsilon_Centauri" title="Epsilon Centauri">&#949;&#160;Centauri</a>. Consequently, &#945;&#160;Centauri itself is known as <span lang="zh" title="Chinese language text">&#21335;&#38272;&#20108;</span> <i>N&#225;n M&#233;n &#200;r</i>, the Second Star of the Southern Gate.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-119"><a href="#cite_note-119">[111]</a></sup>\n</p><p>To the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Australian_aboriginal" title="Australian aboriginal">Australian aboriginal</a> <a href="/wiki/Wergaia" title="Wergaia">Boorong people</a> of northwestern <a href="/wiki/Victoria_(Australia)" title="Victoria (Australia)">Victoria</a>, &#945; Centauri and <a href="/wiki/Beta_Centauri" title="Beta Centauri">&#946; Centauri</a> are <i>Bermbermgle</i>,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-hamacher_120-0"><a href="#cite_note-hamacher-120">[112]</a></sup> two brothers noted for their courage and destructiveness, who speared and killed <i>Tchingal</i> "The Emu" (the <a href="/wiki/Coalsack_Nebula" title="Coalsack Nebula">Coalsack Nebula</a>).<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-stanbridge_121-0"><a href="#cite_note-stanbridge-121">[113]</a></sup> The form in <a href="/wiki/Wergaia" title="Wergaia">Wotjobaluk</a> is <i>Bram-bram-bult</i>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-hamacher_120-1"><a href="#cite_note-hamacher-120">[112]</a></sup>\n</p>\n<div style="clear:both;"></div>\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Future_exploration">Future exploration</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Alpha_Centauri&amp;action=edit&amp;section=21" title="Edit section: Future exploration">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:The_Very_Large_Telescope_and_the_star_system_Alpha_Centauri.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="2550" data-file-width="3840" decoding="async" height="146" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d2/The_Very_Large_Telescope_and_the_star_system_Alpha_Centauri.jpg/220px-The_Very_Large_Telescope_and_the_star_system_Alpha_Centauri.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d2/The_Very_Large_Telescope_and_the_star_system_Alpha_Centauri.jpg/330px-The_Very_Large_Telescope_and_the_star_system_Alpha_Centauri.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d2/The_Very_Large_Telescope_and_the_star_system_Alpha_Centauri.jpg/440px-The_Very_Large_Telescope_and_the_star_system_Alpha_Centauri.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:The_Very_Large_Telescope_and_the_star_system_Alpha_Centauri.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>The Very Large Telescope and Alpha Centauri.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-eso20170109_122-0"><a href="#cite_note-eso20170109-122">[114]</a></sup></div></div></div>\n<div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">See also: <a href="/wiki/2069_Alpha_Centauri_mission" title="2069 Alpha Centauri mission">2069 Alpha Centauri mission</a></div>\n<p>Alpha Centauri is a likely first target for manned or unmanned <a href="/wiki/Interstellar_travel" title="Interstellar travel">interstellar exploration</a>. Using current spacecraft technologies, crossing the distance between the Sun and Alpha Centauri would take several millennia, though the possibility of <a href="/wiki/Nuclear_pulse_propulsion" title="Nuclear pulse propulsion">nuclear pulse propulsion</a> or laser <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Light_sail" title="Light sail">light sail</a> technology, as considered in the <a href="/wiki/Breakthrough_Starshot" title="Breakthrough Starshot">Breakthrough Starshot</a> program, could reduce the journey time to decades.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-NYT-20160412-db_123-0"><a href="#cite_note-NYT-20160412-db-123">[115]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-124"><a href="#cite_note-124">[116]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-125"><a href="#cite_note-125">[117]</a></sup> An objective of such a mission would be to make a fly-by of, and possibly photograph, planets that might exist in the system.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-starshot_126-0"><a href="#cite_note-starshot-126">[118]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-nytimes20160412_127-0"><a href="#cite_note-nytimes20160412-127">[119]</a></sup> The existence of <a href="/wiki/Proxima_Centauri_b" title="Proxima Centauri b">Proxima Centauri b</a>, announced by the <a href="/wiki/European_Southern_Observatory" title="European Southern Observatory">European Southern Observatory</a> (ESO) in August 2016, would be a target for the Starshot program.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-starshot_126-1"><a href="#cite_note-starshot-126">[118]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-nytimes20160824_128-0"><a href="#cite_note-nytimes20160824-128">[120]</a></sup>\n</p><p>In January 2017, Breakthrough Initiatives and the ESO entered a collaboration to search for habitable planets in the Alpha Centauri system. The agreement involves Breakthrough Initiatives providing funding for an upgrade to the <a class="external text" href="https://www.eso.org/public/teles-instr/vlt/vlt-instr/visir/" rel="nofollow">VISIR</a> (VLT Imager and Spectrometer for mid-Infrared) instrument on ESO\'s <a href="/wiki/Very_Large_Telescope" title="Very Large Telescope">Very Large Telescope</a> (VLT) in <a href="/wiki/Chile" title="Chile">Chile</a>. This upgrade will greatly increase the likelihood of planet detection in the system.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-eso20170109_122-1"><a href="#cite_note-eso20170109-122">[114]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-astronomy20170109_129-0"><a href="#cite_note-astronomy20170109-129">[121]</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Distance_estimates">Distance estimates</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Alpha_Centauri&amp;action=edit&amp;section=22" title="Edit section: Distance href="/w/index.php?title=Alpha_Centauri&amp;action=edit&amp;section=24" title="Edit section: Notes">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>\n<div class="reflist" style="list-style-type: decimal;">\n<div class="mw-references-wrap"><ol class="references">\n<li id="cite_note-1"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-1">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text"><a href="/wiki/Proxima_Centauri" title="Proxima Centauri">Proxima Centauri</a> is gravitationally bound to the &#945; Centauri system, but for practical and historical reasons it is described in detail in its own article.</span>\n</li>\n<li id="cite_note-41"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-41">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text"><span class="mwe-math-element"><span class="mwe-math-mathml-inline mwe-math-mathml-a11y" style="display: none;"><math alttext="{\\displaystyle {\\begin{smallmatrix}[(11.2+35.6)/2]^{3}/79.91^{2}=2.0\\end{smallmatrix}}}" xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">\n<semantics>\n<mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">\n<mstyle displaystyle="true" scriptlevel="0">\n<mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">\n<mstyle scriptlevel="1">\n<mtable columnspacing="0.333em" displaystyle="false" rowspacing=".2em">\n<mtr>\n<mtd>\n<mo stretchy="false">[</mo>\n<mo stretchy="false">(</mo>\n<mn>11.2</mn>\n<mo>+</mo>\n<mn>35.6</mn>\n<mo stretchy="false">)</mo>\n<mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">\n<mo>/</mo>\n</mrow>\n<mn>2</mn>\n<msup>\n<mo stretchy="false">]</mo>\n<mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">\n<mn>3</mn>\n</mrow>\n</msup>\n<mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">\n<mo>/</mo>\n</mrow>\n<msup>\n<mn>79.91</mn>\n<mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">\n<mn>2</mn>\n</mrow>\n</msup>\n<mo>=</mo>\n<mn>2.0</mn>\n</mtd>\n</mtr>\n</mtable>\n</mstyle>\n</mrow>\n</mstyle>\n</mrow>\n<annotation encoding="application/x-tex">{\\displaystyle {\\begin{smallmatrix}[(11.2+35.6)/2]^{3}/79.91^{2}=2.0\\end{smallmatrix}}}</annotation>\n</semantics>\n</math></span><img alt="{\\begin{smallmatrix}[(11.2+35.6)/2]^{3}/79.91^{2}=2.0\\end{smallmatrix}}" aria-hidden="true" class="mwe-math-fallback-image-inline" src="https://wikimedia.org/api/rest_v1/media/math/render/svg/8055a4176358ef03e7e2f387877a9ce4a88ed812" style="vertical-align: -0.599ex; margin-bottom: -0.239ex; width:21.325ex; height:2.509ex;"/></span>, see <a href="/wiki/Standard_gravitational_parameter#Two_bodies_orbiting_each_other" title="Standard gravitational parameter">formula</a></span>\n</li>\n<li id="cite_note-53"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-53">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text">This is calculated for a fixed latitude by knowing the star\'s <a href="/wiki/Declination" title="Declination">declination</a> (&#948;) using the formulae (90&#176;+ &#948;). Alpha Centauri\'s declination is &#8722;60&#176; 50&#8242;, so the observed latitude where the star is circumpolar will be south of &#8722;29&#176; 10\'S or 29&#176;. Similarly, the place where Alpha Centauri never rises for northern observers is north of the latitude (90&#176;+ &#948;) N or +29&#176;N.</span>\n</li>\n<li id="cite_note-75"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-75">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text">Proper motions are expressed in smaller angular units than arcsec, being measured in milli-arcsec (mas.) or one-thousandth of an arcsec. Negative values for proper motion in RA indicate the sky motion is from east to west, and in declination north to south.</span>\n</li>\n<li id="cite_note-78"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-78">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text">Changes in position angle (&#952;) are calculated as; <i>&#952;</i>&#160;&#8722;&#160;<i>&#952;</i><sub>o</sub>&#160;=&#160;<i>&#956;</i><sub>&#945;</sub>&#160;&#215;&#160;sin&#160;<i>&#945;</i>&#160;&#215;&#160;(<i>t</i>&#160;&#8722;&#160;<i>t</i><sub>o</sub>&#160;), where; <i>&#945;</i>&#160;= right ascension (in degrees), <i>&#956;</i><sub>&#945;</sub> is the common <a href="/wiki/Proper_motion" title="Proper motion">proper motion</a> (cpm.) expressed in degrees, and <i>&#952;</i> and <i>&#952;</i><sub>o</sub> are the current position angle and calculated position angle at the different epochs.</span>\n</li>\n<li id="cite_note-98"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-98">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text">see Lissauer and Quintana in references below</span>\n</li>\n<li id="cite_note-108"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-108">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text">The coordinates of the Sun would be diametrically opposite Alpha Centauri AB, at <i>&#945;</i>=&#160;02<sup>h</sup>&#160;39<sup>m</sup>&#160;36.4951<sup>s</sup>, <i>&#948;</i>=+60&#176;&#160;50&#8242;&#160;02.308&#8243;</span>\n</li>\n<li id="cite_note-111"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-111">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text">Spellings include <i>Rigjl Kentaurus</i>, <a href="/wiki/Thomas_Hyde" title="Thomas Hyde">Hyde T.</a>, "Ulugh Beighi Tabulae Stellarum Fixarum", <i>Tabulae Long. ac Lat. Stellarum Fixarum ex Observatione Ulugh Beighi</i>, Oxford, 1665, p. 142., Hyde T., "In Ulugh Beighi Tabulae Stellarum Fixarum Commentarii", <i>op. cit.</i>, p. 67., Portuguese <i>Riguel Kentaurus</i> da Silva Oliveira, R., <a class="external text" href="http://www.asterdomus.com.br/Artigo_crux_australis.htm" rel="nofollow">"Crux Australis: o Cruzeiro do Sul"</a> <a class="external text" href="https://web.archive.org/web/20131206102730/http://www.asterdomus.com.br/Artigo_crux_australis.htm" rel="nofollow">Archived</a> 6 December 2013 at the <a href="/wiki/Wayback_Machine" title="Wayback Machine">Wayback Machine</a>, Artigos: Planetario Movel Inflavel AsterDomus.</span>\n</li>\n<li id="cite_note-145"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-145">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text">Weighted parallax based on parallaxes from van Altena <i>et al.</i> (1995) and S&#246;derhjelm (1999).</span>\n</li>\n</ol></div></div>\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="References">References</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Alpha_Centauri&amp;action=edit&amp;section=25" title="Edit section: References">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>\n<div class="reflist columns references-column-width" style="-moz-column-width: 30em;
